--- Commit Message ---
LU-3606 fallocate: Implement fallocate preallocate operation

This patch adds fallocate(2) preallocate operation support
for Lustre. fallocate(2) method of the inode_operations or
file_operations is implemented and transported to the OSTs
to interface with the underlying OSD's fallocate(2) code.

In a saperate patch, a new RPC, OST_FALLOCATE has been
added and reserved for space preallocation. The fallocate
functionality (prealloc) in CLIO has been multiplexed
with CIT_SETATTR. (https://review.whamcloud.com/37277)

Lustre fsx(File system exerciser) is updated in a saperate
patch to handle fallocate calls. (https://review.whamcloud.com/37277)

Only fallocate preallocate operation is supported by this
patch for now. Other operations like, FALLOC_FL_PUNCH
(deallocate), FALLOC_FL_ZERO_RANGE, FALLOC_FL_COLLAPSE_RANGE
and FALLOC_FL_INSPECT_RANGE is not supported by this patch
and will be addressed by a separate patch.

ZFS operation is not supported by this patch. ZFS fallocate(2)
will be addressed by patch (https://review.whamcloud.com/36506/)

New test case under sanity is added to verify fallocate
call.

Test-Parameters: fstype=ldiskfs testlist=sanity,sanityn,sanity-dom

--- Message (Swapnil Pimpale, 2014-04-04 05:22:29.000000000) ---
Patch Set 8:

Hi Jinshan,

I don't mind splitting it into two if that is going to help speed up the review process. Although, it will definitely increase the testing efforts.
Since this patch has already been through one round of review by Andreas and a couple of rounds of review by you do you expect significant changes in the coming patchsets? If yes, I will go ahead and split it.

--- Message (Jinshan Xiong, 2014-04-04 06:04:22.000000000) ---
Patch Set 8:

Hi Swapnil,

Yes, I realize it's really difficult to handle PUNCH case. If the PUNCH area happens to fit into a single osc_extent, the extent will have to be split; or instead we can fill the area out with zeros(a fake PUNCH). Both cases will need a lot of extra work.

So my idea is to split it into two phases: the 1st phase will be focusing on framework and PREALLOC implementation; the 2nd phase is for PUNCH implementation. This patch is already too big, I have to spend over 2 hours to look it through. Therefore splitting it will definitely help produce quality work.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2014-07-22 01:52:10.000000000) ---
Patch Set 15:

Swapnil,
I suspect the problem is that you are sending the full 5MB fallocate() to each object at the 30MB offset, resulting in both objects being 35MB in size == 70MB. 

What should be happening is that the fallocate sends 3MB to the first stripe at 15MB offset, and 2 MB to the second stripe at 15MB offset. 

Jinshan probably can help you better where the calculation of LOV offsets is handled in CLIO, but it should be the same as file writes.

--- Message (Swapnil Pimpale, 2014-07-22 03:32:34.000000000) ---
Patch Set 15:

Calculation of LOV offsets is correct. I verified that by printing the offset and len in ldiskfs_fallocate(). It is as below:
offset: 15728640, len: 3145728
offset: 15728640, len: 2097152

During the testing of falloacte. I came across a bug. I am sharing the output from truncate runs below to highlight the issue.

Issue:
i_blocks after tunncate and fallocate does not get updates/refreshed correctly on the client nodes. Although the server (i_blocks) is correctly updated. This is verified by doing a umount/mount on client to reflect the updated i_blocks. 

Please review.

Thanks

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2019-09-10 05:36:54.000000000) ---
Patch Set 46:

(3 comments)

> Patch was with purpose for landing. I am guessing maybe the "TODO"
 > is causing the confusion. I will remove them.

The part that seemed "not for landing" was all of the hard-coding of fallocate modes in fsx.  I thought the supported FALLOC_FL_* flags would be detected at fsx startup?  Is it possible that the Lustre implementation is not returning the right errors back to the caller?  

We should definitely be returning -EOPNOTSUPP from the client and/or OSD for the FALLOC_FL_* that are not supported.  In particular, we need to return an error for ZERO_RANGE, COLLAPSE_RANGE, and INSPECT_RANGE from the OST until they are handled properly.  Also, we can not support operations like COLLAPSE_RANGE for offsets that are not a multiple of stripe_count * stripe_size, otherwise it would require moving data between OSTs.  That would need to be detected on the client, and for acceptable offsets the remapped offset/range would need to be passed to the OST(s), but for now the client should _also_ return -EOPNOTSUPP for unsupported operations so that the right thing will happen when different client/server versions are in use.  A new client that supports all the modes running against an old server that does not, or an old client without COLLAPSE_RANGE running against a new server that does support additional modes can't depend on the server to return the error.

--- Message (Arshad Hussain, 2019-09-14 11:35:07.000000000) ---

--- Message (Arshad Hussain, 2019-09-14 11:37:02.000000000) ---
Patch Set 37:

(10 comments)

>The part that seemed "not for landing" was all of the hard-coding of >fallocate modes in fsx.  I thought the supported FALLOC_FL_* flags >would be detected at fsx startup?  Is it possible that the Lustre >implementation is not returning the right errors back to the caller?  
Andreas, I see what you mean. The hard coding was done as fsx by default enables "punch holes" and "zero range" etc... To suppress these, specific options like -H needs to be provided. I hard coded these options to be zero (disabled) and let fsx be called regardless of -H or -z options. What I meant was, even if users runs fsx with nothing disabled it will internally still disable it. I think returning -EOPNOTSUPP will make fsx fail. Or second option would be to mandatory pass -H/-z option to suppress punch etc...

I still have these hard-coded. Please do let me know if these must be removed and specific option(like -H/-z) needs to be passed to fsx

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2019-10-09 22:34:15.000000000) ---
Patch Set 53:

I'm meaning to review this again, but haven't had a chance.

One interesting development on the ZFS front is the discussion on whether the "preallocate" operation even makes sense for a copy-on-write filesystem.  I think the only thing that is needed is to ensure that there is enough free space in the filesystem for the fallocate() request, and then (optionally) adjust the file size if FALLOCATE_FL_KEEP_SIZE is not passed.

--- Message (Arshad Hussain, 2019-10-11 16:30:20.000000000) ---
Patch Set 53:

Hi Andreas,
>I'm meaning to review this again, but haven't had a chance.
Thanks as always for reviewing the patch!. Your previous review is still pending. Please hold for new set of reviews :-). I am planning to address your previous review this weekend.

> One interesting development on the ZFS front is the discussion on whether >the "preallocate" operation even makes sense for a copy-on-write >filesystem.  I think the only thing that is needed is to ensure that there >is enough free space in the filesystem for the fallocate() request, and >then (optionally) adjust the file size if FALLOCATE_FL_KEEP_SIZE is not >passed.

Sounds good. Additionally, For mode==0 (standard preallocate), check for available block and adjust the dataset/filesystem stat to reflect space used. Since we pretend that this mode works and actually do not mark the blocks used, this way, we also avoid possibility of other process/thread using up the blocks (space). Which, in such case would lead to preallocate eventually failing with ENOSPC. The reason is the fallocate semantics says that once preallocate'd it is guaranteed that the IO should not fail due to ENOSPC.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2019-10-11 21:52:20.000000000) ---
Patch Set 53:

> Sounds good. Additionally, For mode==0 (standard preallocate),
 > check for available block and adjust the dataset/filesystem stat to
 > reflect space used. Since we pretend that this mode works and
 > actually do not mark the blocks used, this way, we also avoid
 > possibility of other process/thread using up the blocks (space).
 > Which, in such case would lead to preallocate eventually failing
 > with ENOSPC. The reason is the fallocate semantics says that once
 > preallocate'd it is guaranteed that the IO should not fail due to
 > ENOSPC.

It is true that this is what the man page writes, but it is impossible to provide these semantics for ZFS or any copy-on-write filesystem. Even if there is guaranteed spa space for the first write, a second or third write will need extra free space that may not be available, especially if a snapshot is preventing the overwritten blocks from being freed. 

So, it seems that there may be some benefit to ensure the first copy can be written, but I wouldn't try very hard for that to work, just checking the free space is enough to start, to avoid a 1TB fallocate() to succeed when there is only 1MB of free space.

--- Message (Arshad Hussain, 2019-10-12 02:24:29.000000000) ---
Patch Set 53:

>...
>Even if there is guaranteed spa space for the first write, a second or third >write will need extra free space that may not be available, especially if a >snapshot is preventing the overwritten blocks from being freed. 
Andreas, yes this point I overlooked. For any write after 1st, there is still no guarantee. I agree.

>So, it seems that there may be some benefit to ensure the first copy can be >written, but I wouldn't try very hard for that to work, just checking the >free space is enough to start, to avoid a 1TB fallocate() to succeed when >there is only 1MB of free space.
Agreed!

Trevis Autotest retesting enforced review-dne-zfs-part-1 session for build 73521. Requested by Andreas Dilger  because of LU-13400.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2020-04-21 17:29:53.000000000) ---
Patch Set 75: Code-Review-1

(9 comments)

I think the functionality looks good, but I don't think we can disable fsx texting completely for ZFS, or for older servers/clients. That would expose us to data integrity bugs that fsx is good at finding. 

My understanding is that fsx should automatically detect if fallocate() is working on the target filesystem, and we should have the hooks in the client and server to properly report -EOPNOTSUPP if the backing filesystem doesn't support it. If that is not the case, then either something is broken with fsx, or with Lustre, and skipping those tests is just papering over issues that will be seen by end users if they try to use fallocate() in those same environments (eg. ZFS servers or older servers).

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2020-04-21 17:31:15.000000000) ---
